\"text\": \"## LLVM IR Type System to Code Generation Chain\\n\\nThe LLVM type system flows from high-level IR types through SelectionDAG to machine-level types in a multi-stage process:\\n\\n### 1. Type Class Hierarchy (llvm/include/llvm/IR/)\\n\\nThe type system is built on a base Type class (Type.h) with TypeID enum defining all type categories:\\n- **Primitive types**: HalfTyID, FloatTyID, DoubleTyID, VoidTyID, LabelTyID, MetadataTyID\\n- **Derived types**: IntegerTyID, FunctionTyID, PointerTyID, StructTyID, ArrayTyID, FixedVectorTyID, ScalableVectorTyID\\n\\nDerivedTypes.h implements the concrete type classes:\\n- **IntegerType**: Represents arbitrary bit-width integers via IntegerType::get(LLVMContext&, unsigned NumBits)\\n- **FunctionType**: Represents function signatures with return and parameter types, created via FunctionType::get(Type*, ArrayRef<Type*>, bool)\\n- **StructType**: Represents structure types (both literal and identified), created via StructType::get() for literal structs and StructType::create() for identified structs\\n- **ArrayType, VectorType, PointerType**: Additional derived types for arrays, vectors, and pointers\\n\\n### 2. Type Context Ownership (llvm/lib/IR/)\\n\\nType uniqueness is managed by LLVMContext (LLVMContext.h) which owns the implementation object (pImpl) of type LLVMContextImpl (LLVMContextImpl.h).\\n\\nLLVMContextImpl maintains type storage maps:\\n- **IntegerTypes**: DenseMap<unsigned, IntegerType*> storing integer types by bit width\\n- **FunctionTypes**: DenseSet<FunctionType*, FunctionTypeKeyInfo> storing function types with uniqueness based on return type, parameters, and varargs\\n- **AnonStructTypes**: DenseSet<StructType*, AnonStructTypeKeyInfo> for anonymous/literal structs, uniqued by element types and packed bit\\n- **NamedStructTypes**: StringMap<StructType*> for identified/named structs\\n- **ArrayTypes, VectorTypes, PointerTypes**: Similar maps for these derived types\\n\\nThe type creation flow (Type.cpp line 318-340) shows IntegerType::get() checking built-in types first, then looking up custom widths in the context's IntegerTypes map, creating new instances if needed via the context's allocator.\\n\\n### 3. SelectionDAG: Intermediate Representation (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/)\\n\\nSelectionDAG.h declares the SelectionDAG class which represents the mid-level intermediate representation between IR and target-specific machine code. It operates on SDNode objects (SelectionDAGNodes.h) that form a directed acyclic graph.\\n\\nSelectionDAGBuilder (SelectionDAGBuilder.h/cpp) is responsible for converting IR (with IR types) into SelectionDAG nodes. The builder visits IR instructions and creates corresponding DAG nodes, where each node is annotated with machine types (EVT) rather than IR types.\\n\\n### 4. IR Type to Machine Type Lowering\\n\\nThe critical conversion from IR types to machine types happens through:\\n\\n**TargetLowering::getValueType()**:\\n- Located in TargetLowering.h (line 1740-1742)\\n- Takes a DataLayout and an IR Type* pointer\\n- Returns an EVT (Extended Value Type) representing the machine type\\n- Example usage in FastISel.cpp (line 1470): EVT SrcEVT = TLI.getValueType(DL, I->getOperand(0)->getType())\\n\\n**EVT (Extended Value Type)** - ValueTypes.h:\\n- Represents both simple machine types (through embedded MVT) and complex/extended types\\n- Wraps MVT (Machine Value Type) for simple types like i1, i8, i16, i32, i64, f32, f64\\n- Used throughout SelectionDAG for type-checking and type transformations\\n\\n**MVT (Machine Value Type)** - CodeGenTypes/MachineValueType.h:\\n- Represents the actual machine-level types supported by the target\\n- Includes integer sizes (i1-i128), floating point types (f16, f32, f64, f128), vector types\\n- This is the minimal type representation used at the machine code level\\n\\n**LLT (Low Level Type)** - CodeGenTypes/LowLevelType.h:\\n- Alternative low-level type representation used by GlobalISel\\n- Simpler than EVT with explicit scalar and vector information\\n\\n### 5. Type Legalization Pipeline (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/)\\n\\nAfter SelectionDAG construction, types must be legalized to match target capabilities:\\n\\n**LegalizeTypes** (LegalizeTypes.h/cpp):\\n- Core type legalization framework that transforms EVT to legal machine types\\n- Converts unsupported types to combinations of supported types\\n- DAGTypeLegalizer class drives the process\\n\\n**Type-specific legalization**:\\n- LegalizeIntegerTypes.cpp: Handles integer type transformations (promotion, expansion, softening)\\n- LegalizeFloatTypes.cpp: Handles floating-point transformations (softening to integers)\\n- LegalizeVectorTypes.cpp: Handles vector type transformations (splitting, widening, scalarization)\\n- LegalizeDAG.cpp: General DAG operation legalization\\n\\nExample flow (LegalizeTypes.cpp line 432): EVT NewEVT = TLI.getTypeToTransformTo(*DAG.getContext(), OldEVT) transforms an unsupported EVT to a legal equivalent.\\n\\n### Key Data Structure Relationships\\n\\n1. **Type Creation**: User code calls IntegerType::get(Context, 32) → LLVMContextImpl::IntegerTypes[32] is checked/created\\n2. **DAG Building**: SelectionDAGBuilder visits IR with IR types → calls TLI.getValueType(Type*) → EVT\\n3. **Type Legalization**: LegalizeTypes processes EVT → transforms to legal EVT → updates SDNode value types\\n4. **Code Generation**: Legalized SelectionDAG with legal MVT types flows to instruction selection and machine code emission\\n\\n### Critical Files Summary\\n\\n**Type Definition Layer**: Type.h, DerivedTypes.h (class hierarchies)\\n**Type Ownership**: LLVMContext.h, LLVMContextImpl.h (storage and uniquing)\\n**Type Implementation**: Type.cpp (factory methods and type creation logic)\\n**DAG Representation**: \"text\": \"## LLVM IR Type System to Code Generation Chain\\n\\nThe LLVM type system flows from high-level IR types through SelectionDAG to machine-level types in a multi-stage process:\\n\\n### 1. Type Class Hierarchy (llvm/include/llvm/IR/)\\n\\nThe type system is built on a base Type class (Type.h) with TypeID enum defining all type categories:\\n- **Primitive types**: HalfTyID, FloatTyID, DoubleTyID, VoidTyID, LabelTyID, MetadataTyID\\n- **Derived types**: IntegerTyID, FunctionTyID, PointerTyID, StructTyID, ArrayTyID, FixedVectorTyID, ScalableVectorTyID\\n\\nDerivedTypes.h implements the concrete type classes:\\n- **IntegerType**: Represents arbitrary bit-width integers via IntegerType::get(LLVMContext&, unsigned NumBits)\\n- **FunctionType**: Represents function signatures with return and parameter types, created via FunctionType::get(Type*, ArrayRef<Type*>, bool)\\n- **StructType**: Represents structure types (both literal and identified), created via StructType::get() for literal structs and StructType::create() for identified structs\\n- **ArrayType, VectorType, PointerType**: Additional derived types for arrays, vectors, and pointers\\n\\n### 2. Type Context Ownership (llvm/lib/IR/)\\n\\nType uniqueness is managed by LLVMContext (LLVMContext.h) which owns the implementation object (pImpl) of type LLVMContextImpl (LLVMContextImpl.h).\\n\\nLLVMContextImpl maintains type storage maps:\\n- **IntegerTypes**: DenseMap<unsigned, IntegerType*> storing integer types by bit width\\n- **FunctionTypes**: DenseSet<FunctionType*, FunctionTypeKeyInfo> storing function types with uniqueness based on return type, parameters, and varargs\\n- **AnonStructTypes**: DenseSet<StructType*, AnonStructTypeKeyInfo> for anonymous/literal structs, uniqued by element types and packed bit\\n- **NamedStructTypes**: StringMap<StructType*> for identified/named structs\\n- **ArrayTypes, VectorTypes, PointerTypes**: Similar maps for these derived types\\n\\nThe type creation flow (Type.cpp line 318-340) shows IntegerType::get() checking built-in types first, then looking up custom widths in the context's IntegerTypes map, creating new instances if needed via the context's allocator.\\n\\n### 3. SelectionDAG: Intermediate Representation (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/)\\n\\nSelectionDAG.h declares the SelectionDAG class which represents the mid-level intermediate representation between IR and target-specific machine code. It operates on SDNode objects (SelectionDAGNodes.h) that form a directed acyclic graph.\\n\\nSelectionDAGBuilder (SelectionDAGBuilder.h/cpp) is responsible for converting IR (with IR types) into SelectionDAG nodes. The builder visits IR instructions and creates corresponding DAG nodes, where each node is annotated with machine types (EVT) rather than IR types.\\n\\n### 4. IR Type to Machine Type Lowering\\n\\nThe critical conversion from IR types to machine types happens through:\\n\\n**TargetLowering::getValueType()**:\\n- Located in TargetLowering.h (line 1740-1742)\\n- Takes a DataLayout and an IR Type* pointer\\n- Returns an EVT (Extended Value Type) representing the machine type\\n- Example usage in FastISel.cpp (line 1470): EVT SrcEVT = TLI.getValueType(DL, I->getOperand(0)->getType())\\n\\n**EVT (Extended Value Type)** - ValueTypes.h:\\n- Represents both simple machine types (through embedded MVT) and complex/extended types\\n- Wraps MVT (Machine Value Type) for simple types like i1, i8, i16, i32, i64, f32, f64\\n- Used throughout SelectionDAG for type-checking and type transformations\\n\\n**MVT (Machine Value Type)** - CodeGenTypes/MachineValueType.h:\\n- Represents the actual machine-level types supported by the target\\n- Includes integer sizes (i1-i128), floating point types (f16, f32, f64, f128), vector types\\n- This is the minimal type representation used at the machine code level\\n\\n**LLT (Low Level Type)** - CodeGenTypes/LowLevelType.h:\\n- Alternative low-level type representation used by GlobalISel\\n- Simpler than EVT with explicit scalar and vector information\\n\\n### 5. Type Legalization Pipeline (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/)\\n\\nAfter SelectionDAG construction, types must be legalized to match target capabilities:\\n\\n**LegalizeTypes** (LegalizeTypes.h/cpp):\\n- Core type legalization framework that transforms EVT to legal machine types\\n- Converts unsupported types to combinations of supported types\\n- DAGTypeLegalizer class drives the process\\n\\n**Type-specific legalization**:\\n- LegalizeIntegerTypes.cpp: Handles integer type transformations (promotion, expansion, softening)\\n- LegalizeFloatTypes.cpp: Handles floating-point transformations (softening to integers)\\n- LegalizeVectorTypes.cpp: Handles vector type transformations (splitting, widening, scalarization)\\n- LegalizeDAG.cpp: General DAG operation legalization\\n\\nExample flow (LegalizeTypes.cpp line 432): EVT NewEVT = TLI.getTypeToTransformTo(*DAG.getContext(), OldEVT) transforms an unsupported EVT to a legal equivalent.\\n\\n### Key Data Structure Relationships\\n\\n1. **Type Creation**: User code calls IntegerType::get(Context, 32) → LLVMContextImpl::IntegerTypes[32] is checked/created\\n2. **DAG Building**: SelectionDAGBuilder visits IR with IR types → calls TLI.getValueType(Type*) → EVT\\n3. **Type Legalization**: LegalizeTypes processes EVT → transforms to legal EVT → updates SDNode value types\\n4. **Code Generation**: Legalized SelectionDAG with legal MVT types flows to instruction selection and machine code emission\\n\\n### Critical Files Summary\\n\\n**Type Definition Layer**: Type.h, DerivedTypes.h (class hierarchies)\\n**Type Ownership**: LLVMContext.h, LLVMContextImpl.h (storage and uniquing)\\n**Type Implementation**: Type.cpp (factory methods and type creation logic)\\n**DAG Representation**:
